                            <div class="player-info-box-header "><div class="player-info-box-name"><h1>Conor Gillaspie</h1><div class="player-info-box-name-team">&nbsp;</div></div><div class="player-info-box-item">Age: 30</div><div class="player-info-box-item">Bats/Throws: L/R</div>
        <div class="player-info-box-item">6' 1" / 195</div>
        <div class="player-info-box-pos">3B</div></div>
                        <div class="player-info-bio">
                            <strong>Birthdate: </strong>7/18/1987 (30 y, 7 m, 20 d)<br /><b>Drafted:</b> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=9009&position=3B#draft" style="text-decoration:none;">2008 June Amateur Draft - Round: 1s, Pick: 7, Overall: 37, Team: San Francisco Giants</a><br /><strong>Contract:</strong> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=9009&position=3B#contract" >$1.4M / 1 Years (2017)</a>

(8/6/2017)</div></td></tr>

            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

    <tr>
        
        
        
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The Giants drafted Gillaspie in the supplemental round of the 2008 amateur draft and he’s followed a typical path through the minors. In 2011, the third baseman played a full season for the Triple-A Fresno Grizzlies, posting a triple slash of .297/.389/.453 with 11 home runs and nine stolen bases, respectable but by no means outstanding numbers for the Pacific Coast League. Gillaspie is not considered a top prospect for the Giants, falling outside Baseball America’s list of Top 20 for the organization. The infielder is likely to see another full year in Fresno in 2012. (Wendy Thurm)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>A young middle infielder with muted upside is stil a middle infielder. Gillaspie's Major League team also lacks impact middle infielders, so there's an opportunity for him. He'll still probably start the year in the Minor Leagues. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Since being drafted by the Giants in 2008, Gillaspie has made slow, steady progress through the minor leagues. Unfortunately his skill set shows little upside and even in two seasons in the hitter-friendly PCL, he hasn't seen a real growth in the power department. He does display solid plate discipline and he doesn't strike out too often, but that's not going to be enough to earn him more playing time than a cup of coffee or an injury replacement. And now working against him on that front is the fact that Pablo Sandoval doesn't have any more hamate bones to break. (Howard Bender)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Gillaspie finally got a chance to play, and emerged as a useful, yet underwhelming, platoon bat. The White Sox brought in Matt Davidson in the offseason, which should eventually push Gillaspie out of a starting role. If Davidson needs minor league work before beginning the year, Gillaspie would likely platoon with Jeff Keppinger until Davidson is ready. Even though Gillaspie would be on the better side of the platoon, he doesn't do enough to warrant fantasy attention. He's got league-average power without the contact skills or speed to make that package work in fantasy. (<a href="https://twitter.com/Chris_Cwik">Chris Cwik</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Gillaspie is a low upside platoon bat at third. He'll likely be out of a role once Matt Davidson is ready to play in the majors.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>It was a tale of two halves for Conor Gillespie. He hit .326/.377/.484 over the first half, posting solid peripherals. Things imploded down the stretch. Gillaspie hit just .228/.284/.330 in the second half. As usual, batted ball luck played a big role in his performance. During the first half, he showed a ridiculous .370 batting average on balls in play. Over the second half, that figure dropped to .265. In most of the these cases, the easiest thing to do is assume his talent lies somewhere in the middle. While third base isn’t the strongest fantasy spot, Gillaspie comes with two concerns going forward. He doesn’t hit lefties, and so would be platooned in an ideal world, and his ability to hit home runs faded last season. It’s unclear if that’s due to his declining home run rate, or if Gillaspie just has doubles power. His upside is pretty limited, meaning he won’t be a starter in all but the deepest of leagues. He’s the type of player who can help you get by for a couple of weeks, or fill a spot cheaply in a deep league, but that’s it. (<a href="https://twitter.com/Chris_Cwik">Chris Cwik</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Gillaspie had an up and down year. While he wasn’t as bad as he showed over the second half, his flaws keep him from being a starter in all but the deepest of leagues.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Are you lost or having some schadenfreude? The 28-year-old Gillaspie looks to be done as a major league regular as he tries to find a new home this offseason. Maybe I am being a little harsh on him, but none of his traits point to a positive outcome. He has a ~5% home run per fly ball ratio over the past two seasons with 11 total homers. He has never shown much speed (zero career stolen bases). Gillaspie is a free swinger, but has a career batting average on balls in play under .300. Even worse, his defensive value has been declining over the past three seasons to a -10 Ultimate Zone Rating at third in 67 games. He may need to move to first base for his glove. The problem is a player who hits like a bad backup catcher is not going to cut it at first. I would not be surprised if he starts the 2016 season in the minors or in indie ball. (Jeff Zimmerman)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Conor Gillaspie’s productive days are past him. He probably needs to move to first base, but his bat will not be good enough for the majors at that position.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Profile:  Gillaspie came through big for the Giants in the Wild Card game with a game-winning home run. Still, Gillaspie projects to be a bench player for the Giants with Eduardo Nuñez slated to start at third. Gillapsie posted a career-best isolated power, yet his .178 ISO is nothing to get very excited about as he totaled 18 extra-base hits in 205 plate appearances. That number was driven by 4 triples, which is not a career-best in volume, but his triple rate is the best he’s had in his career. Gillaspie has seen his walk percentage drop the past two seasons as he has not been above 6% during that time despite posting a career mark of 7%. In 2015, it appeared his plate approach was trending in the wrong direction as his strikeout percentage jumped up to 19%. In 2016, he improved his K% to 14% (a career-best), which is once again encouraging and still not enough to expect a breakout. There were improvements in his game last season, but it’s hard to say that these will sustain based on 205 PA and it’s doubtful he will see much more than that this season in order to make him somebody looked at beyond your deepest fantasy leagues. (Paul Kastava)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Gillaspie saw a boost in his power and a drop in his strikeout rate in a small sample. Playing time will be tough to come by in order to see if these gains are legitimate and would make a potential impact in even deeper fantasy leagues.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
</table>

			<th scope="col" class="rgHeader">Season</th><th scope="col" class="rgHeader">Team</th><th scope="col" class="rgHeader" style="text-align:right;"><a href="javascript:doNothing();"
